<div id="review_585877648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/585877648" />
    <a title="Danny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3254909-danny"><img alt="Danny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301556302p2/3254909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/585877648?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danny" href="/user/show/3254909-danny">Danny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer585877648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8326875113654546900"><a href='http://bewitchedbookworms.com/2013/08/wild-cards-by-simone-elkeles.html' rel='nofollow noopener'> Read Review at Bewitched Bookworms</a><br/><br/>Simone Elkeles is just an amazing Author and her books just belong to my must-buy-must-read list. I love her contemporary stories and I lover her happy ends. When I found out about her new series about Football players I was barely able to hold back from jumping up and down. Ever since watching Friday Night Lights I am a HUGE fan of American Football!!<br/><br/> <br/><br/>Characters made of Awesome!<br/>The story is actually told from two POV, one is Ashlyn and one is Derek…. And .. I </span>
  <span id="freeText8326875113654546900" style="display:none"><a href="http://bewitchedbookworms.com/2013/08/wild-cards-by-simone-elkeles.html" rel="nofollow noopener"> Read Review at Bewitched Bookworms</a><br /><br />Simone Elkeles is just an amazing Author and her books just belong to my must-buy-must-read list. I love her contemporary stories and I lover her happy ends. When I found out about her new series about Football players I was barely able to hold back from jumping up and down. Ever since watching Friday Night Lights I am a HUGE fan of American Football!!<br /><br /> <br /><br />Characters made of Awesome!<br />The story is actually told from two POV, one is Ashlyn and one is Derek…. And .. I couldn’t love those two any more! No, I can’t!!! (Yep, we need a lot of exclamation marks!) But were impressive characters that totally and fully and completely made their way into my heart.<br /><br />Lets first talk about Ashlyn!<br />Ash is one of the few girls who play football together with the boys, and…. She’s good! She’s really good and all her Teammates loves and support her! But Ash is definitely not a Tomboy – she can also be super sexy and girly. I loved that about her. She has as many girl friends as she has boy friends and she easily got along with all of them! On top of this she has spunk! Yes, this girl doesn’t take crap from anyone and is strong, focused and determined!<br /><br />Now… let’s take a moment to swoon over Derek.<br />*Swoon*<br /><br />I cannot love Derek anymore and I want him to be my Book Boyfriend! Now, girls – see? I called totally dips here!<br /><br />Derek was rebellious, but not too much to be annoying. But. After the death of his mother he lost his focus and rather played pranks than taking anything seriously. But, there is so much more about him. The way he interacted with his stepmother and especially his little kid brother was breaking my heart it was so damn sweet!<br /><br />But, I mostly enjoyed Derek’s attitude! The way he constantly teased Ash and constantly challenged her and it drove her nuts! He’s a little arrogant but since we also get glimpses of his thoughts we know that he just likes to put this wall of arrogance around himself.<br /><br /> <br /><br />Sizzling hot romance and heartbreaking vulnerability<br />Both Ash and Derek do not have an easy life and in turn they are both looking for something different in a relationship. Both think they just don’t match even though they are obviously attracted to each other. The chemistry was sizzling and they got under each others skin like no one before, yet they are both afraid about the deeper feelings they develop.<br /><br />Gosh I loved their love story.So.Freaking.Much! It was beautiful, hot and also sometimes heartbreaking. Both are so vulnerable especially when it comes to admitting real feelings and I found it to be raw but it was never overdone and never over the top!<br /><br /> <br /><br />Now, I can’t finish without talking about the overall storyline and the football themed plot. The story was just great, it showed the wonderful friendship between the teammates and their admiration for Ash. But also Derek’s part of the story was just wonderful.<br /><br />Now – please bring on the next book.Now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8326875113654546900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_695186300" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/695186300" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/695186300?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer695186300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12017818369813149645">This review also appears on <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2013/10/22/wild-cards-by-simone-elkeles-review-a-lovehate-antagonistic-romance/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews!<br/><br/>Derek is a bad boy who has been unwillingly relocated to Chicago by his ditzy stepmother. He meets his new stepsister, a gorgeous tomboy who is the captain of her football team. Instantly attracted to each other, but not seeming to get along, the two undergo a love/hate relationship throughout the course of the book.<br/><br/>Wild Cards is filled with romance cliches, instant love, to an extremely good looking boy and girl, to an </span>
  <span id="freeText12017818369813149645" style="display:none">This review also appears on <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2013/10/22/wild-cards-by-simone-elkeles-review-a-lovehate-antagonistic-romance/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews!<br /><br />Derek is a bad boy who has been unwillingly relocated to Chicago by his ditzy stepmother. He meets his new stepsister, a gorgeous tomboy who is the captain of her football team. Instantly attracted to each other, but not seeming to get along, the two undergo a love/hate relationship throughout the course of the book.<br /><br />Wild Cards is filled with romance cliches, instant love, to an extremely good looking boy and girl, to an obstacle of them not being able to be together for various reasons. The incredible overuse of synonyms was scattered throughout - Derek is described with shaggy brown hair, totally ripped, mesmerizing clear blue eyes, a deep masculine voice, a bronzed chest and perfect physique. Ashtyn on the other hand, "talks like a jock but has a body like an angel". It's over-exaggerated and totally hilarious.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the snarky, sarcastic dialogue and Derek and Ashtyn's antagonistic relationship. Derek's playful, carefree and confident attitude was the perfect balance to Ashtyn's stubborn, spunky and headstrong personality and it was fun seeing the two tease each other with witty comments. The two are obviously attracted to each other, and didn't admit their feelings until they'd wound each other up. It was frustrating seeing them get close and then pull away, retreating into their shells because they don't think they are each other's type.<br /><br />I'm supposed to keep my emotions in check and only hook up with girls who want a good time, not girls who are desperate to make this something more than it could ever be. - Derek<br /><br />It was refreshing to have a female in a traditionally male dominated role, and you could see what part of Ashtyn's personality made her perfect for being the football captain. Unfortunately her inner dialogue began to grate after a while, showing off how insecure she really was.<br /><br />I don't want a guy who cringes at the thought of having a real relationship instead of a one-night stand. - Ashtyn<br /><br />Wild Cards started out really strong but began to fizzle towards the end, when it became melodramatic and angsty as the two tried to stay away from each other. The last quarter of had a heavy football focus and I began to tune out. Despite its flaws, Wild Cards took me by surprise, it was the light fluffy read I was looking for after some heavy dystopians. That's probably why some of the cliches didn't bother me much, I just laughed at them and continued to enjoy the book.<br /><br />I received this book for review from Bloomsbury Australia and Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />Series: Wild Cards #1<br /><br />Rating: 3 out of 5</span>
  <a data-text-id="12017818369813149645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1365840469" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1365840469" />
    <a title="Gertiebee * the little book bee *" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19569054-gertiebee-the-little-book-bee"><img alt="Gertiebee * the little book bee *" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375405176p2/19569054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1365840469?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gertiebee * the little book bee *" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gertiebee * the little book bee *" href="/user/show/19569054-gertiebee-the-little-book-bee">Gertiebee * the little book bee *</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19569054-gertiebee-the-little-book-bee?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19569054-gertiebee-the-little-book-bee?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1365840469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10227686632731442187"> <br/> <i>
  <b>3 Girl-kicking-ass-in-a-boy-dominated-sport Stars</b>
</i><br/><br/>When I was younger, I played a sport called <b>"Aussie rules/ footy"</b> (aka Australian football). <br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439783520ra/15884165.gif' width='400' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439786035ra/15884501.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439785865ra/15884478.gif' width='400' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I played for fun ( I wasn't good at it ) and dropped out to focus on my passions.<br/><br/>So what am I rambling about this for? Well, this story brought up a memory of a girl I played the game with. She was fantastic at Woman's Aussie football. She was magic on the field, it was her passion and it showed.<br/><br/>But, she faced the same problem as the main charact</span>
  <span id="freeText10227686632731442187" style="display:none"> <br> <i>
  <b>3 Girl-kicking-ass-in-a-boy-dominated-sport Stars</b>
</i><br><br>When I was younger, I played a sport called <b>"Aussie rules/ footy"</b> (aka Australian football). <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439783520ra/15884165.gif" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439786035ra/15884501.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439785865ra/15884478.gif" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I played for fun ( I wasn't good at it ) and dropped out to focus on my passions.<br><br>So what am I rambling about this for? Well, this story brought up a memory of a girl I played the game with. She was fantastic at Woman's Aussie football. She was magic on the field, it was her passion and it showed.<br><br>But, she faced the same problem as the main character in this story. Apart from the team she played with- no one supported her.<b> So, that girl gave up on football and pursued what was expected of her</b>.<br><br>How many girls do not pursue sports they are good at, because:<br><br><b>They have no support</b><br><br><i>“If your mother were here, she’d never allow you to be on the football team. She’d sign you up for cooking classes or dance classes or something like that.” <br>Ashtyn looks like his words are a slap in the face. “I like football, Dad. I’m good at it. If you’d come to a game or practice and just watch me . . .” Her voice trails to a whisper as Gus dismisses her words and walks to his car."</i><br><br><b>It's male dominated AND they are not taken seriously</b><br><br><i> “We won’t tolerate sexual harassment of any kind. If you feel harassed at any time, inform me or anyone else on staff. That being said, I hope you have a thick skin. Boys will be boys. Don’t jump the gun, if you know what I mean.”<br><br>"I straighten my shoulders and move to the end of the check-in line. I’m aware of a couple of stares from players and some parents. I’m a girl playing a boy’s sport, and while my team has gotten used to having a female teammate, some guys don’t believe girls should play football. They think we’re too fragile. I just have to keep my head held high and act like I belong here as much as they do. Derek’s words echo in my head: You can do this. A couple of guys in front of me nudge each other, urging their friends to gawk at the lone girl in line.”</i><br><br><b>Why three stars?</b><br><br>1) The Football- I liked that Ash didn't have a typical dream. A girl becoming captain of the football team is unheard of. That said, there wasn't even one football game!!! <br><br>2) Insta-love- There are rare occasions when insta-love works and this wasn't one of them.<br><br>Overall, a quick read that has a great premise BUT is executed dismally.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10227686632731442187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_973737996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/973737996" />
    <a title="Lindsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5302761-lindsey"><img alt="Lindsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590442791p2/5302761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/973737996?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey" href="/user/show/5302761-lindsey">Lindsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=favorite-author">favorite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=awesome-female-lead">awesome-female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=bad-ass-heroine">bad-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=alpha-male-to-the-max">alpha-male-to-the-max</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=sports-romance">sports-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer973737996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16510100419275644392">Let me first start off with the fact that I am not a football fan at all, so I was very reluctant to read this. I actually hated all the football players in high school, or anyone else who was considered 'popular'. <br/><br/>However, Simone has this divine talent to get me to adore all her teenage angst. This book had pretty much every element I adore in my young adult fiction. Every character I adored, right down to the dippy step-mother. She was dippy but she was endearing. Ashtyn was an amazing lead fe</span>
  <span id="freeText16510100419275644392" style="display:none">Let me first start off with the fact that I am not a football fan at all, so I was very reluctant to read this. I actually hated all the football players in high school, or anyone else who was considered 'popular'. <br /><br />However, Simone has this divine talent to get me to adore all her teenage angst. This book had pretty much every element I adore in my young adult fiction. Every character I adored, right down to the dippy step-mother. She was dippy but she was endearing. Ashtyn was an amazing lead female that was smart, strong, and stood up to the dynamics that were tossed at her as a high school female that plays footballs. <br /><br />Her ex-boyfriend situation was hard for me to stomach but I understand her reactions to everything. I loved Derek from the start and I was totally routing for him and Ashtyn right off the bat. It is very hard for me to express myself in this review because there wasn't any part of it that bothered me. The flow of the book was perfect and kept you engaged from beginning to end. The rise and fall in the drama left the reader both happy and ugly crying when the you know what really hit the fan. <br /><br />If you love young adult fiction, and are a fan of Abbi Glines then I highly recommend this book! <br /><br />*I got a FREE copy of this book from my local library*</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer604144263441369759"><b>COVER REVEAL!</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1368194466l/13065327.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>

</b><br/><i><br/>After getting kicked out of boarding school, bad boy Derek Fitzpatrick has no choice but to live with his ditzy stepmother while his military dad is deployed. Things quickly go from bad to worse when he finds out she plans to move them back to her childhood home in Illinois. Derek’s counting the days before he can be on his own, and the last thing he needs is to get involved with someone else’s family drama.<br/><br/>Ashtyn Parker knows one thing for certain--people you care about le</i></span>
  <span id="freeText604144263441369759" style="display:none"><b>COVER REVEAL!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1368194466l/13065327.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>Blurb</i>
</b><br><i><br>After getting kicked out of boarding school, bad boy Derek Fitzpatrick has no choice but to live with his ditzy stepmother while his military dad is deployed. Things quickly go from bad to worse when he finds out she plans to move them back to her childhood home in Illinois. Derek’s counting the days before he can be on his own, and the last thing he needs is to get involved with someone else’s family drama.<br><br>Ashtyn Parker knows one thing for certain--people you care about leave without a backward glance. A football scholarship would finally give her the chance to leave. So she pours everything into winning a state championship, until her boyfriend and star quarterback betrays them all by joining their rival team. Ashtyn needs a new game plan, but it requires trusting Derek—someone she barely knows, someone born to break the rules. Is she willing to put her heart on the line to try and win it all?<br></i></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ELiWgkAEcBohD+RnPPfshVPoMOpEKlVy8Qbh+W3T/PwcgTfczl7SE+nuxz6g2aTQXjgTXwHr02iBCz6i9hq+gw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MiwUkPvmh87IeHZSTvSAeVfKgaKei6p39242zjzcckA+FbXOdbwlxwCZVQvS2sgsWhqiF9tKLG2HY+mVpxUwPw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11367458817316210775">Simone Elkeles is a <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of novels for teens. Simone’s books have won many awards including being YALSA Top Ten Quick Picks for Reluctant Young Adult Readers, being named to the YALSA Popular Paperbacks and Teens Top Ten lists, and added to the Illinois “Read for a Lifetime” Reading List. Simone also won the coveted RITA award from the Romance Writers of </span>
  <span id="freeText11367458817316210775" style="display:none">Simone Elkeles is a <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of novels for teens. Simone’s books have won many awards including being YALSA Top Ten Quick Picks for Reluctant Young Adult Readers, being named to the YALSA Popular Paperbacks and Teens Top Ten lists, and added to the Illinois “Read for a Lifetime” Reading List. Simone also won the coveted RITA award from the Romance Writers of America for her book Perfect Chemistry. Simone is especially proud of the fact that the Illinois Association of Teachers of English named her Author of the Year. <br /><br />Simone was born and raised in the suburbs of Chicago, where she still lives today. Simone went to the University of Illinois in Urbana-Champaign and received her Bachelor’s of Science there in Psychology in 1992. She continued her education at Loyola University-Chicago where she received her Master’s of Science degree in Industrial Relations while working for a manufacturing company creating diversity programs for their employees.<br /><br />She loves animals (she has two dogs – a labradoodle and a German Shepherd), kids (she also has two of those) and her family. In her spare time she’s the Hockey Mom for her kids hockey teams and is an active Girl Scout leader specially trained in outdoor education. She also spends time mentoring other teen and adult authors. (She also loves sushi, which you can probably tell by reading her books.) Simone writes about teens because she was a teen in the 80’s (when spiked hair and blue eye shadow were “rad”) and she loves writing about those exciting teen relationships and romances.</span>
